if(google_ads.length
!=
0)
{








apply_ad_config(google_ads.length);









render_ads(true,
window['ad_config_top']);









if(window['backfillParam'])
{












window['backfillParam']['pl_rnum']
=
google_ads.length;












window['backfillParam']['pl_time']
=
Date.now()
-
afc_ad_start_time;








}




}
}

function
apply_ad_config(num)
{
window['ad_config_top']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
window['ad_config_bot']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
}

google_ad_client
=
'ca-aj-cat';
google_ad_channel
=
'cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN';
google_ad_output
=
'js';
google_max_num_ads
=
'4';
google_ad_type
=
'text';
google_image_size
=
'';
google_num_ads_recieved=
'';
google_language
=
'';
google_country
=
'';
google_encoding
=
'utf8';
google_safe
=
'medium';
google_adtest
=
'off';
google_ad_section
=
'default';
google_page_url
=
'';
google_hints
=
'Garbage_(band)';
google_kw
=
'';
google_kw_type
=
'broad';


var
backfillParam
=
{




pl_rqnum
:
google_max_num_ads,




pl_hints
:
google_hints,




pl_rp
:
"false",




pl_kw
:
google_kw,




pl_cl
:
google_ad_client,




pl_ch
:
google_ad_channel,




pl_hex
:
"#FDFEEE",




pl_type
:
"afc",




pl_clksp
:
"none"};

var
word_arr
;

var
word_arr_len
;


function
highlightQuery(input_str)
{

var
queryTokenArray
=
"band,(,_,),garbage,";


var
tok_arr
=
queryTokenArray.split(",");

for(tok_arr_idx=0;
tok_arr_idx
<
tok_arr.length-1;
tok_arr_idx
++)
{

if(isCombinationWord(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx])){
word_arr
=
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].split("-");
word_arr_len
=
word_arr.length;
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],0);

if(first_pos
!=-1)
{
input_str
=
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos);
}
}
else
{
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],0);
if(first_pos
!=
-1
&&
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].length
>
0)
{
input_str
=
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],first_pos);
}
}
}
return
input_str;
}

function
isCombinationWord(word){
if(word.indexOf("-")
!=
-1){
return
true;
}
else
{
return
false;
}
}


function
isAlpha(ch)
{
if
(ch
!=
null
&&
ch.match(/^[a-zA-Z0-9]+$/)){
return
true;
}
return
false;
}

function
isQueryinInput(firstindex,
input_str,
j){
for(i=firstindex;
i<
input_str.length
;
++i)
{
var
currindex
=
i;

if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(i)))
{
if(firstindex
==
currindex)

{
firstindex++;
}
else
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
if
(j
==
word_arr_len-1)
return
currindex;
else
return
isQueryinInput(currindex+1,input_str,++j);
}
}
}

if(j
<
word_arr_len)
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex+1).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
}

return
(currindex
+
1)
;
}


function

highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos)
{
exactmatch
=
isQueryinInput(first_pos+word_arr[0].length,input_str,1)
;
if(exactmatch
!=-1
)

{
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,exactmatch)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(exactmatch);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],exactmatch+7);
while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,next_pos);
}
}
return
input_str;
}


function

highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,
first_pos)
{
var
end_pos
=
first_pos
+
token.length;
if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(end_pos))
&&
!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(first_pos-1))){
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,end_pos)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(end_pos);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos+7);
}
else
{
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos);
}

while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,next_pos);
}
return
input_str;
}</script>

<p><b>Garbage</b>
is
a
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
music">rock</a>
band
formed
in
<a
href="/wiki/Madison,_Wisconsin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Madison,
Wisconsin">Madison,
Wisconsin</a>,
in
1994.<sup
id="cite_ref-behindthemusic_4-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-behindthemusic-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
group
consists
of
Scottish
singer
<a
href="/wiki/Shirley_Manson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Shirley
Manson">Shirley
Manson</a>
(vocals,
guitar)
and
American
musicians
<a
href="/wiki/Duke_Erikson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Duke
Erikson">Duke
Erikson</a>
(bass,
guitar,
keyboards,
percussion),
<a
href="/wiki/Steve_Marker?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Steve
Marker">Steve
Marker</a>
(guitar,
keyboards),
and
<a
href="/wiki/Butch_Vig?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Butch
Vig">Butch
Vig</a>
(drums,
percussion).
All
four
members
are
involved
in
<a
href="/wiki/Songwriting?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Songwriting"
class="mw-redirect">songwriting</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Record_producer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Record
producer">production</a>.
The
band
have
counted
worldwide
album
sales
of
over
17
million
units.<sup
id="cite_ref-Famous_Scots_Exhibition.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Shirley_Manson_.28News_Release.29_5-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Famous_Scots_Exhibition.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Shirley_Manson_.28News_Release.29-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Garbage
released
a
string
of
increasingly
successful
<a
href="/wiki/Single_(music)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Single
(music)">singles</a>
in
1995–1996,
including
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Stupid_Girl_(Garbage_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stupid
Girl
(Garbage
song)">Stupid
Girl</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Only_Happy_When_It_Rains?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Only
Happy
When
It
Rains">Only
Happy
When
It
Rains</a>&quot;.
Their
debut
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Garbage_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Garbage
(album)">Garbage</a></i>,
was
an
<a
href="/wiki/Sleeper_hit?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sleeper
hit">unexpected
smash</a>,
selling
over
4
million
copies
and
certified
<a
href="/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Music
recording
sales
certification">double
platinum</a>
in
the
UK,
US,
and
Australia.
Garbage
won
the
Breakthrough
Artist
award
at
the
1996
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Europe
Music
Awards">MTV
Europe
Music
Awards</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Version2.0PR_6-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Version2.0PR-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Garbage
spent
two
years
working
on
follow-up
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Version_2.0?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Version
2.0">Version
2.0</a></i>,
which
topped
the
<a
href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="UK
Albums
Chart">charts
in
the
UK</a>
upon
its
1998
release
and
the
following
year
was
nominated
for
two
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award">Grammy
Awards</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Album_of_the_Year?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Album
of
the
Year">Album
of
the
Year</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rock_Album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
Rock
Album">Best
Rock
Album</a>.
<i>Version
2.0</i>
went
on
to
match
the
sales
of
its
predecessor.
Garbage
followed
this
up
by
performing
and
co-producing
<a
href="/wiki/The_World_Is_Not_Enough_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
World
Is
Not
Enough
(song)">the
theme
song</a>
to
the
nineteenth
<a
href="/wiki/James_Bond?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="James
Bond">James
Bond</a>
movie
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_World_Is_Not_Enough?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
World
Is
Not
Enough">The
World
Is
Not
Enough</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-BGPR_7-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-BGPR-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Despite
being
named
one
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone">Rolling
Stone</a>'</i>s
Top
10
Albums
of
the
Year,<sup
id="cite_ref-RSBG_8-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RSBG-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
Garbage's
2001
third
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Beautiful_Garbage?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Beautiful
Garbage">Beautiful
Garbage</a></i>
failed
to
match
the
commercial
success
achieved
by
its
predecessors.<sup
id="cite_ref-BleedPR_9-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-BleedPR-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
Garbage
quietly
disbanded
in
late
2003,
but
regrouped
to
complete
fourth
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Bleed_Like_Me?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bleed
Like
Me">Bleed
Like
Me</a></i>
in
2005,
peaking
at
a
career-high
No.&nbsp;4
in
the
US.<sup
id="cite_ref-AGsleevenotes_10-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AGsleevenotes-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
cut
short
their
concert
tour
in
support
of
<i>Bleed
Like
Me</i>
announcing
an
&quot;indefinite
hiatus&quot;,<sup
id="cite_ref-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup>
emphasizing
that
they
had
not
broken
up,
but
wished
to
pursue
personal
interests.<sup
id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_12-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
2006,
Vig
returned
to
producing
while
Manson
worked
on
an
as
yet
unreleased
solo
album.
Garbage
ended
their
hiatus
in
2007
and
released
<a
href="/wiki/Greatest_hits?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Greatest
hits"
class="mw-redirect">greatest
hits</a>
retrospective
<i><a
href="/wiki/Absolute_Garbage?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Absolute
Garbage">Absolute
Garbage</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_13-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
Garbage's
fifth
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Not_Your_Kind_of_People?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Not
Your
Kind
of
People">Not
Your
Kind
of
People</a></i>
was
released
in
2012
via
the
band's
own
independent
label,
Stunvolume
Records.<sup
id="cite_ref-NME_14-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-NME-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<div
style="overflow:hidden;height:;">








&nbsp;







</div>

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="History">History</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Garbage_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1"
title="Edit
section:
History">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Formation_and_early_years_.281993.E2.80.931994.29">Formation
and
early
years
(1993–1994)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Garbage_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2"
title="Edit
section:
Formation
and
early
years
(1993–1994)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Duke
Erikson
and
Butch
Vig
had
been
in
numerous
bands,
including
<a
href="/wiki/Spooner_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Spooner
(band)">Spooner</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Fire_Town?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fire
Town">Fire
Town</a>
(with
Steve
Marker
as
a
<a
href="/wiki/Sound_engineer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sound
engineer"
class="mw-redirect">sound
engineer</a>).
In
1983,
Vig
and
Marker
founded
<a
href="/wiki/Smart_Studios?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Smart
Studios">Smart
Studios</a>
in
Madison
and
Vig's
production
work
brought
him
to
the
attention
of
<a
href="/wiki/Sub_Pop?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sub
Pop">Sub
Pop</a>.
Spooner
reunited
in
1990
and
released
another
record,
but
disbanded
in
1993
as
Vig
and
Marker's
career
as
producers
gained
strength.<sup
id="cite_ref-RecordCollector_15-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RecordCollector-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1994,
as
Vig
become
&quot;kind
of
burned
out
on
doing
really
long
records,&quot;
he
got
together
with
Erikson
and
Marker,
and
they
started
doing
remixes
for
acts
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/U2?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="U2">U2</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Depeche_Mode?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Depeche
Mode">Depeche
Mode</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Nine_Inch_Nails?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nine
Inch
Nails">Nine
Inch
Nails</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/House_of_Pain?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="House
of
Pain">House
of
Pain</a>.
The
remixes
featured
different
instrumentation,
and
often
highlighting
new
guitar
hooks
and
bass
grooves.
This
experience
inspired
the
three
men
to
form
a
band,
where
they
&quot;wanted
to
take
that
remix
sensibility
and
somehow
translate
it
into
all
of
the
possibilities
of
a
band
setup.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-sos_16-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-sos-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
An
early
comment
that
their
work
sounded
&quot;like
garbage&quot;
inspired
the
band's
name.<sup
id="cite_ref-behindthemusic_4-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-behindthemusic-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Initial
sessions
with
Vig
on
vocals,
along
with
the
members'
past
work
with
all-male
groups,
led
to
the
band's
desire
for
a
woman
on
lead.<sup
id="cite_ref-volume_17-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-volume-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
Marker
declared
that
their
desire
for
a
female
vocalist
was
one
&quot;who
didn't
have
a
high,
chirpy,
girly
quality
to
her
voice&quot;,
similar
to
<a
href="/wiki/Patti_Smith?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Patti
Smith">Patti
Smith</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Chrissie_Hynde?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chrissie
Hynde">Chrissie
Hynde</a>,
and
Vig
added
that
they
wanted
someone
that
could
sing
in
an
understated
way
in
contrast
to
&quot;these
alterna-rock
singers
[that]
have
a
tendency
to
<a
href="/wiki/Screaming_(music)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Screaming
(music)">scream</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-18"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
Marker
was
watching
<i><a
href="/wiki/120_Minutes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="120
Minutes">120
Minutes</a></i>
when
he
saw
the
music
video
for
<a
href="/wiki/Angelfish_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Angelfish
(band)">Angelfish</a>'s
&quot;Suffocate
Me&quot;.
He
showed
the
video
to
Erikson
and
Vig
while
their
manager
Shannon
O'Shea
tracked
down
the
band's
singer,
Shirley
Manson.
When
Manson
was
contacted,
she
did
not
know
who
Vig
was
and
was
urged
to
check
the
<a
href="/wiki/Credit_(creative_arts)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Credit
(creative
arts)">credits</a>
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/Nevermind?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nevermind">Nevermind</a></i>,
the
popular
<a
href="/wiki/Nirvana_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nirvana
(band)">Nirvana</a>
album
which
Vig
produced.<sup
id="cite_ref-behindthemusic_4-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-behindthemusic-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
April
8,
1994,
Manson
met
Erikson,
Marker,
and
Vig
for
the
first
time
in
London.
Later
that
evening
Vig
was
informed
of
Nirvana
frontman
<a
href="/wiki/Kurt_Cobain?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kurt
Cobain">Kurt
Cobain</a>'s
suicide.<sup
id="cite_ref-behindthemusic_4-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-behindthemusic-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
Garbage
was
put
on
hold
until
Angelfish
was
finished
touring
North
America
in
support
of
<a
href="/wiki/Live_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live
(band)">Live</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-TFYUS_19-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-TFYUS-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup>
Erikson,
Marker,
and
Vig
attended
the
<a
href="/wiki/Metro_Chicago?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Metro
Chicago">Metro
Chicago</a>
date,
and
Manson
was
invited
to
Madison
to
audition
for
the
band.
The
audition
did
not
go
well,
but
Manson
socialized
with
the
men
while
there
and
they
found
they
had
a
similar
taste
in
music.
Angelfish
disbanded
at
the
end
of
the
Live
tour.
Manson
called
O'Shea
and
asked
to
audition
again
feeling
that
&quot;it
would
work
out&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-behindthemusic_4-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-behindthemusic-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Manson
described
her
first
session
with
the
band
as
&quot;a
disaster&quot;,
as
she
had
no
experience
as
a
<a
href="/wiki/Session_musician?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Session
musician">session
musician</a>,
and
she
and
the
band
were
&quot;two
parties
totally
uncomfortable
with
the
situation&quot;,
but
the
&quot;mutual
disdain&quot;
from
that
meeting
managed
to
pull
the
band
together.
The
first
songs
were
skeletal
versions
of
the
songs
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Stupid_Girl_(Garbage_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stupid
Girl
(Garbage
song)">Stupid
Girl</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Queer_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Queer
(song)">Queer</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Vow_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vow
(song)">Vow</a>&quot;,
which
led
to
some
ad-libbed
lyrics
by
Manson.<sup
id="cite_ref-Serendipitous_20-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Serendipitous-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-makingmusic_21-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-makingmusic-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup>
Manson
had
never
written
a
song
prior
to
this
session;
nevertheless,
this
time
she
was
invited
to
join
the
band.<sup
id="cite_ref-behindthemusic_4-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-behindthemusic-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
Lyrics
were
penned
at
a
cabin
in
the
north
woods
of
Wisconsin
while
the
songs
were
recorded
at
Smart
Studios.<sup
id="cite_ref-garbagepr_22-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-garbagepr-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup>
Conscious
of
the
grunge
genre
that
had
made
their
names,
particularly
Vig's,
the
band
made
every
effort
to
avoid
sounding
similar,
deliberately
striving
to
make
a
<a
href="/wiki/Pop_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pop
music">pop</a>
record.<sup
id="cite_ref-23"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Garbage
sent
out
<a
href="/wiki/Demo_(music)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Demo
(music)">demo
tapes</a>
with
no
bio,
to
avoid
a
bidding
war
over
Vig's
production
history.<sup
id="cite_ref-recordcollector_24-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-recordcollector-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup>
Garbage
signed
with
<a
href="/wiki/A%26E_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="A&amp;E
Records">Mushroom
UK</a>
worldwide
(excluding
North
America)
and
secured
the
band
a
<i><a
href="/wiki/Volume_magazine?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Volume
magazine"
class="mw-redirect">Volume</a></i>
magazine
compilation
inclusion.<sup
id="cite_ref-25"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
only
potential
candidate
for
release
was
&quot;Vow&quot;,
as
it
was
the
only
song
for
which
the
band
had
completed
production.<sup
id="cite_ref-volume_17-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-volume-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
When
released
in
December,
&quot;Vow&quot;
began
to
receive
<a
href="/wiki/Radio_airplay?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Radio
airplay"
class="mw-redirect">radio
airplay</a>
on
<a
href="/wiki/XFM?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="XFM">XFM</a>
and
from
<a
href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_1?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="BBC
Radio
1">Radio
1</a>
DJs
<a
href="/wiki/Steve_Lamacq?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Steve
Lamacq">Steve
Lamacq</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/John_Peel?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Peel">John
Peel</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Johnnie_Walker_(DJ)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Johnnie
Walker
(DJ)">Johnnie
Walker</a>.
<a
href="/wiki/Word-of-mouth?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Word-of-mouth"
class="mw-redirect">Word-of-mouth</a>
on
&quot;Vow&quot;
took
the
track
back
to
the
US.<sup
id="cite_ref-26"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
December
21,
Garbage
signed
to
<a
href="/wiki/Jerry_Moss?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jerry
Moss">Jerry
Moss</a>'s
label
<a
href="/wiki/Almo_Sounds?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Almo
Sounds">Almo
Sounds</a>
for
North
America.<sup
id="cite_ref-Shirleycontract_27-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Shirleycontract-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup>
Manson
was
licensed
to
both
Mushroom
and
Almo
by
Radioactive
Records
for
a
single
album,
with
no
compensation
from
any
of
Garbage's
labels.<sup
id="cite_ref-28"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Garbage
had
not
even
considered
&quot;Vow&quot;
for
inclusion
on
the
album
or
even
as
a
single.<sup
id="cite_ref-musician_29-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-musician-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup>
Because
the
exclusive
licensing
of
<i>Volume</i>
prevented
a
full
commercial
single
release,<sup
id="cite_ref-garbagepr_22-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-garbagepr-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup>
on
March
20,
1995,
Mushroom
issued
&quot;Vow&quot;
in
a
limited
<a
href="/wiki/7%22_vinyl?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="7&quot;
vinyl"
class="mw-redirect">7&quot;
vinyl</a>
format
through
Discordant,
a
label
set
up
just
to
launch
Garbage.<sup
id="cite_ref-OHWIRsell-in_30-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-OHWIRsell-in-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup>
By
May,
commercial
alternative
radio
in
the
US
had
picked
up
on
the
track,
and
it
began
to
receive
heavy
rotation
nationwide.<sup
id="cite_ref-31"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;Vow&quot;
debuted
on
<a
href="/wiki/Modern_Rock_Tracks?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Modern
Rock
Tracks"
class="mw-redirect">Hot
Modern
Rock
Tracks</a>
at
No.&nbsp;39.
It
climbed
gradually
over
the
following
weeks,
peaking
at
No.&nbsp;26
on
July.<sup
id="cite_ref-vow_32-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-vow-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;Vow&quot;
<a
href="/wiki/Bubbling_Under_Hot_100_Singles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bubbling
Under
Hot
100
Singles">bubbled
under</a>
for
two
weeks
before
it
spent
two
weeks
on
the
Billboard
Hot
100
staying
at
No.&nbsp;97
both
weeks.<sup
id="cite_ref-vow_32-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-vow-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-bubble_33-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bubble-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Garbage_.281995.E2.80.931997.29"><i>Garbage</i>
(1995–1997)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Garbage_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3"
title="Edit
section:
Garbage
(1995–1997)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
August
1995,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Garbage_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Garbage
(album)">Garbage</a></i>
debuted
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_200?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
200">Billboard
200</a>
at
No.&nbsp;193.
In
the
United
Kingdom,
its
release
was
preceded
by
non-album
track
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Subhuman_(Garbage_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Subhuman
(Garbage
song)">Subhuman</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Only_Happy_When_It_Rains?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Only
Happy
When
It
Rains">Only
Happy
When
It
Rains</a>&quot;
as
singles
to
promote
the
album
instead
of
&quot;Queer&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-OHWIRsell-in_30-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-OHWIRsell-in-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
debuted
on
the
UK
album
chart
at
No.&nbsp;12.<sup
id="cite_ref-MusicWeek05_34-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MusicWeek05-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
Australia,
the
album
debuted
at
No.&nbsp;5.<sup
id="cite_ref-version2.0POS_35-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-version2.0POS-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;Queer&quot;
was
quickly
released
in
the
UK
and
Europe,
while
Garbage
began
their
first
tour.
Garbage
was
nominated
for
<a
href="/wiki/Brit_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brit
Awards">Brit
Awards</a>
for
Best
New
Band
and
Best
International
Newcomer.<sup
id="cite_ref-KerrangBritAwards_36-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-KerrangBritAwards-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Garbage
toured
for
the
self-titled
<i>Garbage</i>
throughout
1996.
&quot;Only
Happy
When
It
Rains&quot;
was
released
as
a
single
in
North
America;
&quot;Stupid
Girl&quot;
was
released
to
promote
European
dates.
MTV
announced
that
&quot;Only
Happy
When
It
Rains&quot;
was
certified
a
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Buzz_Bin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Buzz
Bin">Buzz
clip</a>&quot;,
guaranteeing
heavy
rotation
on
its
network
from
February
13.<sup
id="cite_ref-NMEFilth_37-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-NMEFilth-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;Only
Happy&quot;
peaked
at
No.&nbsp;55
on
the
Hot
100.<sup
id="cite_ref-38"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;Stupid
Girl&quot;
received
frequent
video
and
radio
<a
href="/wiki/Airplay_(radio)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Airplay
(radio)"
class="mw-redirect">airplay</a>
in
the
UK
and
peaked
at
No.&nbsp;4,
becoming
the
band's
first
top
10
hit
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="UK
Singles
Chart">UK
Singles
Chart</a>
and
elevated
the
album
to
No.&nbsp;6.<sup
id="cite_ref-BGPromo_39-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-BGPromo-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
May,
Garbage
reworked
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Milk_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Milk
(song)">Milk</a>&quot;
with
<a
href="/wiki/Tricky_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tricky
(musician)">Tricky</a>
in
a
<a
href="/wiki/Chicago?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chicago">Chicago</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Recording_studio?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Recording
studio">recording
studio</a>
before
supporting
<a
href="/wiki/Smashing_Pumpkins?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Smashing
Pumpkins"
class="mw-redirect">Smashing
Pumpkins</a>
on
their
arena
tour
until
the
<a
href="/wiki/Drug_overdose?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Drug
overdose">overdose</a>
of
Pumpkins
keyboardist
<a
href="/wiki/Jonathan_Melvoin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jonathan
Melvoin">Jonathan
Melvoin</a>.
&quot;Stupid
Girl&quot;
peaked
at
No.&nbsp;24
on
the
Hot
100.<sup
id="cite_ref-40"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup>
Its
<a
href="/wiki/Contemporary_hit_radio?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Contemporary
hit
radio">Top
40
radio</a>
remix
by
<a
href="/wiki/Todd_Terry?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Todd
Terry">Todd
Terry</a>
received
massive
airplay.<sup
id="cite_ref-Hits_41-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Hits-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Worldwide,
the
final
single
release
from
the
album
was
the
reworked
version
of
&quot;Milk&quot;,
which
became
the
band's
second
UK
top
10
hit.
The
band
performed
the
song
live
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Europe
Music
Awards">MTV
Europe
Music
Awards</a>
in
London
on
November
14;
Garbage
won
the
Breakthrough
award
at
the
event.<sup
id="cite_ref-Momonov96_42-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Momonov96-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
North
America,
Almo
Sounds
released
album
track
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Supervixen?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Supervixen">Supervixen</a>&quot;
to
Modern
Rock
radio,<sup
id="cite_ref-43"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup>
while
<a
href="/wiki/Capitol_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Capitol
Records">Capitol
Records</a>
released
a
remix
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Number_One_Crush?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Number
One
Crush">#1
Crush</a>&quot;
from
the
soundtrack
to
<i><a
href="/wiki/Romeo_%2B_Juliet?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Romeo
+
Juliet">Romeo
+
Juliet</a></i>,
which
topped
the
<a
href="/wiki/Alternative_Songs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alternative
Songs">Modern
Rock
Tracks</a>
chart
for
four
weeks
from
the
end
of
the
year;
the
remix
was
also
featured
as
the
theme
for
the
TV
show
<a
href="/wiki/Hex_(TV_series)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hex
(TV
series)"><i>Hex</i></a>.
&quot;#1
Crush&quot;
was
later
nominated
for
Best
Song
From
a
Movie
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/1997_MTV_Movie_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="1997
MTV
Movie
Awards">1997
MTV
Movie
Awards</a>.</p>








<p><i><a
href="/wiki/Garbage_Video?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Garbage
Video">Garbage
Video</a></i>,
a
compilation
of
the
album's
<a
href="/wiki/Music_video?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Music
video">promotional
videos</a>,
was
released
in
November
1997.<sup
id="cite_ref-Momonov96_42-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Momonov96-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup>
Garbage
was
nominated
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_New_Artist?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
New
Artist">Grammy
Award
for
Best
New
Artist</a>,
while
&quot;Stupid
Girl&quot;
received
two
nominations
for
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rock_Song?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
Rock
Song">Best
Rock
Song</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rock_Performance_by_a_Duo_or_Group_with_Vocal?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
Rock
Performance
by
a
Duo
or
Group
with
Vocal">Best
Rock
Performance
By
A
Duo
Or
Group</a></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Version_2.0_.281997.E2.80.932000.29"><i>Version
2.0</i>
(1997–2000)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Garbage_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4"
title="Edit
section:
Version
2.0
(1997–2000)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Garbage
relocated
to
<a
href="/wiki/Friday_Harbor?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Friday
Harbor"
class="mw-redirect">Friday
Harbor</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Washington_(state)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Washington
(state)">Washington</a>
on
March
1,
1997
to
write
songs
for
their
second
album.
Returning
to
Smart
Studios
a
short
while
later,
the
band
found
themselves
under
intense
pressure
to
repeat
the
success
of
<i>Garbage</i>.
The
band
decided
not
to
change
their
formula,
but
progress
musically
by
pushing
their
sound
as
far
as
it
could
go—hence
the
album's
eventual
title
<i><a
href="/wiki/Version_2.0?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Version
2.0">Version
2.0</a></i>,
which
was
completed
by
February
15,
1998.
In
March,
the
first
single
&quot;Push
It&quot;
became
the
No.&nbsp;1
most
added
record
at
the
UK
Alternative
Radio.<sup
id="cite_ref-Fastfacts_44-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Fastfacts-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
became
their
third
consecutive
UK
top
ten
hit
at
No.&nbsp;9.<sup
id="cite_ref-BGPromo_39-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-BGPromo-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-ussingles_45-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ussingles-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
May
1998,
<i>Version
2.0</i>
debuted
at
No.&nbsp;1
in
the
UK
and
at
No.&nbsp;13
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_200?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
200"><i>Billboard</i>
200</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-MusicWeek05_34-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MusicWeek05-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-46"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup>
Garbage
began
touring
<i>Version
2.0</i>
that
month,
a
tour
which
lasted
until
the
end
of
1999.
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Think_I%27m_Paranoid?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Think
I'm
Paranoid">I
Think
I'm
Paranoid</a>&quot;
was
released
worldwide
in
July,
while
the
music
video
for
&quot;Push
It&quot;
received
eight
nominations
at
the
1998
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Video
Music
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">MTV
Video
Music
Awards</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-47"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup>
By
October
12,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Special_(Garbage_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Special
(Garbage
song)">Special</a>&quot;
was
released
and
Garbage
was
nominated
for
three
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Europe
Music
Awards">MTV
Europe
Music
Awards</a>:
&quot;Best
Group&quot;,
&quot;Best
Rock
Act&quot;
and
&quot;Best
Video&quot;
for
&quot;Push
It&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Fastfacts_44-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Fastfacts-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
early
1999,
<i>Version
2.0</i>
received
two
Grammy
Award
nominations
for
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Album_of_the_Year?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Album
of
the
Year">Album
of
the
Year</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rock_Album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
Rock
Album">Best
Rock
Album</a><sup
id="cite_ref-48"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;Special&quot;
was
No.&nbsp;1
most
added
single
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Top_40_radio?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Top
40
radio"
class="mw-redirect">Top
40
radio</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Fastfacts_44-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Fastfacts-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_49-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
Europe,
Garbage
began
their
biggest
headline
tour,
releasing
singles
for
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/When_I_Grow_Up_(Garbage_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="When
I
Grow
Up
(Garbage
song)">When
I
Grow
Up</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Trick_Is_to_Keep_Breathing?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Trick
Is
to
Keep
Breathing">The
Trick
Is
to
Keep
Breathing</a>&quot;.
In
April,
&quot;When
I
Grow
Up&quot;
was
released
to
Modern
Rock
radio.<sup
id="cite_ref-autogenerated5_50-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-autogenerated5-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;When
I
Grow
Up&quot;
was
then
featured
on
the
movie
<i><a
href="/wiki/Big_Daddy_(1999_film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Big
Daddy
(1999
film)">Big
Daddy</a></i>.
<i>Version
2.0</i>
was
awarded
the
European
Platinum
Award
by
the
<a
href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_the_Phonographic_Industry?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="International
Federation
of
the
Phonographic
Industry">International
Federation
of
the
Phonographic
Industry</a>
for
1
million
sales
across
Europe
and
US.<sup
id="cite_ref-Fastfacts_44-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Fastfacts-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/You_Look_So_Fine?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="You
Look
So
Fine">You
Look
So
Fine</a>&quot;
was
released
as
the
final
single
from
<i>Version
2.0</i>
worldwide,
as
Garbage
toured
Europe,
including
headlining
in
Edinburgh
to
mark
the
opening
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Scottish
Parliament">Scottish
Parliament</a>.</p>








<p>On
August
4,
Garbage
was
contracted
to
perform
the
theme
for
the
James
Bond
film
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_World_Is_Not_Enough?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
World
Is
Not
Enough">The
World
Is
Not
Enough</a></i>
and
worked
with
composer
<a
href="/wiki/David_Arnold?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="David
Arnold">David
Arnold</a>
in
London
and
<a
href="/wiki/Vancouver?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-51"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup>
Garbage
co-headlined
an
Australian
tour
with
<a
href="/wiki/Alanis_Morissette?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alanis
Morissette">Alanis
Morissette</a>,
while
&quot;When
I
Grow
Up&quot;
spent
three
months
in
the
Australian
chart,
becoming
the
band's
most
successful
single
there.<sup
id="cite_ref-YLSFpress_52-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-YLSFpress-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_World_Is_Not_Enough_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
World
Is
Not
Enough
(song)">The
World
Is
Not
Enough</a>&quot;
reached
the
top
10s
in
Italy,
Latvia,
Lithuania,
Norway
and
Finland,
as
well
as
the
top
40
in
Germany,
Austria,
Switzerland
and
the
UK.<sup
id="cite_ref-YLSFpress_52-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-YLSFpress-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;Special&quot;
received
Grammy
nominations
for
Best
Rock
Song
and
for
Best
Rock
Performance
by
a
Duo
or
Group,
while
&quot;When
I
Grow
Up&quot;
was
re-issued
in
Europe.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Beautiful_Garbage_.282001.E2.80.932002.29"><i>Beautiful
Garbage</i>
(2001–2002)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Garbage_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5"
title="Edit
section:
Beautiful
Garbage
(2001–2002)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:222px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Shirley_Manson.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Shirley_Manson.jpg/220px-Shirley_Manson.jpg"
width="220"
height="238"
class="thumbimage"
srcset="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Shirley_Manson.jpg/330px-Shirley_Manson.jpg
1.5x,
http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Shirley_Manson.jpg/440px-Shirley_Manson.jpg
2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Shirley_Manson.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img

/></a>










</div>
Shirley
Manson
performing
live
at
Voodoo
Festival
2002









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>Garbage
regrouped
on
April
10,
2001.
The
group
began
work
on
their
third
record,
and
put
aside
plans
for
a
<a
href="/wiki/B-sides?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="B-sides"
class="mw-redirect">B-sides</a>
album
due
to
the
sale
of
Almo
Sounds
to
the
<a
href="/wiki/Universal_Music_Group?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Universal
Music
Group">UMG</a>.
Manson
ran
an
online
blog
throughout
the
recording
of
the
album
named
<i><a
href="/wiki/Beautiful_Garbage?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Beautiful
Garbage">Beautiful
Garbage</a></i>.
During
the
recording
of
the
album,
Garbage
invoked
a
provision
of
its
contract
to
leave
Almo,
and
sued
UMG
when
it
refused
to
terminate
the
contract.
UMG
threatened
to
use
Manson's
1993
solo
contract
to
tie
Garbage
to
the
label.<sup
id="cite_ref-53"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
suit
was
settled
on
July
29,
2001,
and
Garbage
moved
to
<a
href="/wiki/Interscope?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Interscope"
class="mw-redirect">Interscope</a>.
Lead
single
&quot;Androgyny&quot;
was
released
to
radio
by
the
end
of
August,
and
its
video
was
released
on
September
10.<sup
id="cite_ref-BGInterscopePOSbrochure_54-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-BGInterscopePOSbrochure-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
following
day,
due
to
the
<a
href="/wiki/September_11_attacks?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="September
11
attacks">September
11
attacks</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/New_York_City?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
York
City">New
York
City</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Washington_D.C?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Washington
D.C"
class="mw-redirect">Washington
D.C</a>,
the
promotional
schedule
for
the
album
was
put
on
hold.<sup
id="cite_ref-55"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Released
three
weeks
after
the
<a
href="/wiki/September_11_attacks?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="September
11
attacks">September
11
attacks</a>,
the
album
suffered
from
lack
of
promotion,
mixed
reaction
from
critics
and
fans
alike,
and
the
failure
of
its
<a
href="/wiki/Lead_single?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lead
single">lead
single</a>
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Androgyny_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Androgyny
(song)">Androgyny</a>&quot;
to
achieve
high
chart
positions.<sup
id="cite_ref-56"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup>
Despite
faltering
in
major
markets,
<i>Beautiful
Garbage</i>
debuted
at
No.&nbsp;1
on
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
(magazine)"><i>Billboard</i></a>'s
<a
href="/wiki/Top_Electronic_Albums?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Top
Electronic
Albums"
class="mw-redirect">Top
Electronic
Albums</a>
chart
where
it
stayed
for
8
weeks,<sup
id="cite_ref-57"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup>
topped
the
album
charts
in
<a
href="/wiki/Australia?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Australia">Australia</a>,
and
was
named
one
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone">Rolling
Stone</a>'</i>s
&quot;Top
10
Albums
of
the
Year&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-autogenerated6_58-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-autogenerated6-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
October,
<i>Beautiful
Garbage</i>
achieved
a
No.&nbsp;13
debut
on
the
Billboard
200,<sup
id="cite_ref-59"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup>
as
well
as
reaching
No.&nbsp;6
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Top_Internet_Albums?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Top
Internet
Albums"
class="mw-redirect">Top
Internet
Albums</a>
chart
and
topping
the
Electronic
Albums
chart
for
seven
weeks.
In
its
first
three
months
on
sale,
<i>Beautiful
Garbage</i>
sold
1.2
million
copies.<sup
id="cite_ref-60"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Garbage
supported
<a
href="/wiki/U2?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="U2">U2</a>
on
the
third
leg
of
their
<a
href="/wiki/Elevation_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Elevation
Tour">Elevation
Tour</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-U2_61-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-U2-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
the
last
show,
Vig
contracted
<a
href="/wiki/Hepatitis_A?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hepatitis
A">Hepatitis
A</a>
and
was
replaced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Matt_Chamberlain?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Matt
Chamberlain">Matt
Chamberlain</a>
for
European
dates.
In
December
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Breaking_Up_the_Girl?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Breaking
Up
the
Girl">Breaking
Up
the
Girl</a>&quot;
was
released
as
a
single
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Theme_song?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Theme
song"
class="mw-redirect">theme
song</a>
to
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Daria?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Daria">Daria</a></i>
<a
href="/wiki/Telemovie?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Telemovie"
class="mw-redirect">telemovie</a>
<i><a
href="/wiki/Is_It_College_Yet%3F?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Is
It
College
Yet?">Is
It
College
Yet?</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-RSBG_8-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RSBG-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
December
27,
<i>Rolling
Stone'</i>s
US
and
Australian
editions
named
<i>Beautiful
Garbage</i>
as
one
of
their
<a
href="/wiki/Critics?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Critics"
class="mw-redirect">critics</a>
&quot;Top
10
Albums
of
the
Year&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-RSBG_8-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RSBG-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Cherry_Lips?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cherry
Lips">Cherry
Lips</a>&quot;
was
released
at
the
end
of
2001,
becoming
a
massive
hit
in
Australia,
peaking
at
number
seven
on
the
ARIA
Charts,
and
number
eleven
in
the
highly
influential
<a
href="/wiki/Triple_J_Hottest_100,_2001?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Triple
J
Hottest
100,
2001">Triple
J
Hottest
100,
2001</a>.
<a
href="/wiki/Sony_Music_Japan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sony
Music
Japan"
class="mw-redirect">Sony
Music
Japan</a>
released
an
exclusive
E.P.
of
rare
tracks
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Special_Collection_(Garbage_E.P.)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Special
Collection
(Garbage
E.P.)"
class="mw-redirect">Special
Collection</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-BGJapan_62-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-BGJapan-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Bleed_Like_Me_.282003.E2.80.932005.29"><i>Bleed
Like
Me</i>
(2003–2005)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Garbage_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6"
title="Edit
section:
Bleed
Like
Me
(2003–2005)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Garbage
started
proper
work
on
their
fourth
record
in
March
2003,
writing
&quot;Right
Between
the
Eyes&quot;
in
30
minutes.
It
was
a
false
start.<sup
id="cite_ref-Geffen_63-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Geffen-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup>
Recording
for
the
album
was
halted
during
the
summer
when
singer
Shirley
Manson
underwent
surgery
on
her
right
<a
href="/wiki/Vocal_cord?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vocal
cord"
class="mw-redirect">vocal
cord</a>
and
was
not
given
the
okay
to
sing
again
until
August.<sup
id="cite_ref-BLMjournal_64-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-BLMjournal-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup>
By
October,
due
to
rising
tension
within
the
band
and
a
breakdown
in
communication<sup
id="cite_ref-65"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup>
Vig
relocated
to
<a
href="/wiki/Los_Angeles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Los
Angeles">Los
Angeles</a>
while
Manson
returned
to
<a
href="/wiki/Scotland?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Scotland">Scotland</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-BLMEPK_66-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-BLMEPK-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup>
During
the
<a
href="/wiki/Christmas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Christmas">Christmas</a>
period,
Vig
encountered
excited
Garbage
fans
eager
to
hear
how
the
album
was
going.
Not
having
the
heart
to
tell
them
Garbage
had
effectively
split,
he
name-dropped
titles
to
them.
After
this
encounter
he
realized
there
was
still
something
left
in
the
band.<sup
id="cite_ref-BLMEPK_66-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-BLMEPK-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
January
2004
Garbage
reconvened
in
Los
Angeles
with
<a
href="/wiki/Dust_Brothers?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dust
Brothers">Dust
Brother</a>
<a
href="/wiki/John_King_(producer)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
King
(producer)">John
King</a>,
drummer
Matt
Chamberlain,
bassist
<a
href="/wiki/Justin_Meldal-Johnsen?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Justin
Meldal-Johnsen">Justin
Meldal-Johnsen</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-67"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
on
February
6,
<a
href="/wiki/Dave_Grohl?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dave
Grohl">Dave
Grohl</a>
performed
drums
on
&quot;Bad
Boyfriend&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-68"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup>
His
performance
was
regarded
by
the
band
as
&quot;raising
the
bar&quot;
for
the
record.<sup
id="cite_ref-BLMEPK_66-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-BLMEPK-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup>
Following
the
John
King
sessions,
the
band
formally
relocated
to
<a
href="/wiki/Los_Angeles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Los
Angeles">Los
Angeles</a>
and
wrote
two
new
songs,
&quot;Metal
Heart&quot;
and
&quot;Boys
Wanna
Fight&quot;,<sup
id="cite_ref-BLMEPK_66-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-BLMEPK-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup>
which
were
more
energetic
songs
than
the
band
had
been
writing
as
well
as
lyrically
more
&quot;overtly
political&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-BLMEPK_66-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-BLMEPK-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup>
both
songs
referencing
the
US
and
UK
led
<a
href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="2003
invasion
of
Iraq">2003
invasion
of
Iraq</a>.</p>








<p>In
2005,
lead
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Why_Do_You_Love_Me?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Why
Do
You
Love
Me">Why
Do
You
Love
Me</a>&quot;
debuted
on
the
Modern
Rock
Tracks
chart
at
No.&nbsp;39.<sup
id="cite_ref-69"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup>
as
well
as
No.&nbsp;97
and
No.&nbsp;81
on
the
Billboard
Hot
100
and
<a
href="/wiki/Pop_100?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pop
100">Pop
100</a>
charts
respectively,
becoming
the
band's
most
successful
single
for
six
years.
<i>Bleed
Like
Me</i>
entered
Top
10
in
US.<sup
id="cite_ref-70"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
August
25,
2005
Garbage
cancelled
their
scheduled
October
tour
dates
in
France,
Belgium
and
United
Kingdom
and
released
a
statement
that
the
band
had
&quot;somewhat
overextended
themselves&quot;
and
had
decided
to
conclude
their
tour
in
Australia
on
October
1.<sup
id="cite_ref-71"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup>
Upfront
of
the
band's
Australian
tour,
&quot;Sex
Is
Not
The
Enemy&quot;
was
released
to
Australian
radio.<sup
id="cite_ref-72"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
end
of
the
Australian
tour
marked
the
end
of
active
promotion
for
<i>Bleed
Like
Me</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-73"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
confirmed
that
they
were
going
&quot;on
indefinite
hiatus&quot;
to
dispel
reports
of
a
band
split.<sup
id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_12-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Absolute_Garbage_.282007.E2.80.932008.29"><i>Absolute
Garbage</i>
(2007–2008)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Garbage_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7"
title="Edit
section:
Absolute
Garbage
(2007–2008)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Garbage
ended
their
18-month
hiatus
on
January
31,
2007,
at
a
benefit
show
in
<a
href="/wiki/Glendale,_California?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Glendale,
California">Glendale</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/California?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="California">California</a>,
organised
by
Vig
to
help
pay
musician
<a
href="/wiki/Wally_Ingram?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wally
Ingram">Wally
Ingram</a>'s
medical
care
following
treatment
for
<a
href="/wiki/Esophageal_cancer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Esophageal
cancer">throat
cancer</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_13-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
Prior
to
this,
Garbage
had
been
sharing
song
ideas
via
the
internet
and
were
keen
on
getting
into
the
recording
studio
to
complete
them.<sup
id="cite_ref-74"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup>
Garbage
began
work
on
the
new
songs
in
earnest
during
February
and
March
at
Vig's
home
studio,<sup
id="cite_ref-ButchVigInterview_75-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ButchVigInterview-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup>
completing
four
tracks
including
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Tell_Me_Where_It_Hurts_(Garbage_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tell
Me
Where
It
Hurts
(Garbage
song)">Tell
Me
Where
It
Hurts</a>&quot;,
which
was
released
as
the
album's
lead
single.</p>








<p><i><a
href="/wiki/Absolute_Garbage?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Absolute
Garbage">Absolute
Garbage</a></i>
was
released
in
July,
remastered
and
including
a
special
edition
bonus
remix
package.
A
DVD
format
rounded
out
the
package;
among
the
fifteen
Garbage
music
videos
included
was
a
documentary
film
titled
&quot;Thanks
For
Your,
Uhhh
Support&quot;
featuring
backstage
and
behind-the-scenes
footage,
live
performances
and
interviews.<sup
id="cite_ref-76"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup>
Vig
stated
that
Garbage
was
considering
mid-2008
to
begin
making
a
fifth
album,
saying,
&quot;We're
thinking
about
it...
I
think
we're
more
interested
in
making
something
that's
much
more
primal
and
stripped
down.
<i>Absolute
Garbage</i>
is
the
postscript
to
chapter
one.
Whatever
we
do
next
will
definitely
be
chapter
two&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-77"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
May
2008,
it
was
announced
that
Manson
would
be
joining
the
cast
of
US
TV
show
<i><a
href="/wiki/Terminator:_The_Sarah_Connor_Chronicles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Terminator:
The
Sarah
Connor
Chronicles">Terminator:
The
Sarah
Connor
Chronicles</a></i>
in
a
regular
role.<sup
id="cite_ref-78"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup>
A
Garbage
track
called
“Witness
to
Your
Love”
was
released
on
a
charity,
“limited
availability,”
compilation
in
the
US.
The
release
was
available
from
<a
href="/wiki/Urban_Outfitters?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Urban
Outfitters">Urban
Outfitters</a>
from
Wednesday,
October
15,
2008,
to
Thursday,
January
31,
2009,
and
went
on
radio
in
the
US
on
October
17.<sup
id="cite_ref-79"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-80"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Not_Your_Kind_of_People_and_recent_activity_.282010.E2.80.93present.29"><i>Not
Your
Kind
of
People</i>
and
recent
activity
(2010–present)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Garbage_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8"
title="Edit
section:
Not
Your
Kind
of
People
and
recent
activity
(2010–present)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>On
February
1,
2010,
it
was
confirmed
through
Shirley
Manson's
official
<a
href="/wiki/Facebook?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Facebook">Facebook</a>
profile
that
she
spent
a
week
in
the
studio
with
her
bandmates.<sup
id="cite_ref-facebook_81-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-facebook-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
the
post,
Manson
wrote
&quot;Guess
who
I
just
spent
a
week
in
the
studio
with?
Would
you
be
pleased
if
I
said
one
of
them
was
called
Steve
and
one
of
them
was
called
Duke
and
another
was
a
Grammy-winning
producer?&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-facebook_81-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-facebook-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
October
2010,
it
was
officially
confirmed
that
Garbage
were
recording
their
fifth
studio
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-heraldscotland.com_82-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-heraldscotland.com-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
September
17,
2011,
the
band
clarified
that
their
forthcoming
11-track
<a
href="/wiki/Long_player?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Long
player"
class="mw-redirect">LP</a>
would
be
mixed
by
October
17,
while
another
12
songs
will
be
finalized
by
the
end
of
the
year
and
see
release
as
&quot;b-sides,
extra
tracks
and
maybe
one
might
even
come
your
way
simply
as
a
Christmas
present
from
Garbage
as
a
thank
you
to
you
all
for
sticking
around,&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-clarify_83-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-clarify-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup>
though
this
did
not
materialize.</p>








<p>The
band
announced
to
<i><a
href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
(magazine)">Billboard</a></i>
that
their
fifth
studio
album
will
be
released
independently
of
any
major
label
support,
with
Vig
confirming,
&quot;We're
looking
at
this
as
free
agents.
We're
out
of
all
our
corporate
responsibilities
from
the
past,
and
initially
we
thought
that
was
terrifying
but
now
we
think
it's
liberating.
We're
going
to
put
the
record
out
on
our
own
label
and
just
figure
out
how
to
license
it
and
market
it
because
we
want
it
under
our
control.&quot;
Vig
also
stated
that
the
group
would
tour
in
support
of
the
record.<sup
id="cite_ref-Billboard2011_84-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Billboard2011-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
another
interview
with
<i><a
href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Spin
(magazine)">Spin</a></i>,
lead
singer
Shirley
Manson
stated,
&quot;People
we've
played
it
for
[have
said]
it
sounds
like
the
first
record,
and
I'm
thinking
to
myself,
'It
doesn't
sound
anything
like
the
first
record,'
but
there
is
an
energy
there
that's,
I
think,
reminiscent
of
the
first
record;
a
sort
of
hungriness
is
there,&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-Spin2011_85-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Spin2011-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup>
while
Vig
told
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone">Rolling
Stone</a></i>,
&quot;I
think
you
can
hear
some
energy
and
a
vibe
in
the
tracks
that
sounds
refreshing
-
a
little
bit
more
to
me
like
the
first
two
records.
Somehow
we
have
a
collective
sound.
When
we
spin
the
ideas
through
the
four
of
our
brains
it
comes
out
and
it's
kind
of
a
thing
that's
identifiable.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-RollingStone2011_86-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RollingStone2011-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
January
6,
2012,
the
band
announced
that
they
had
entered
Red
Razor
Studios
in
<a
href="/wiki/Glendale,_California?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Glendale,
California">Glendale,
California</a>
to
record
bonus
material
for
their
forthcoming
album,<sup
id="cite_ref-87"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup>
later
confirming
on
Twitter
that
a
further
five
tracks
were
being
worked
on,
including
the
new
title
&quot;What
Girls
Are
Made
Of.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-88"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p><i><a
href="/wiki/Not_Your_Kind_of_People?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Not
Your
Kind
of
People">Not
Your
Kind
of
People</a></i>
was
released
on
May
14,
2012,
reaching
number
13
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_200?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
200"><i>Billboard</i>
200</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-USInfo_89-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-USInfo-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
number
10
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="UK
Albums
Chart">UK
Albums
Chart</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-MusicWeekSales_90-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MusicWeekSales-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
supported
the
album
with
the
year-long
<a
href="/wiki/Not_Your_Kind_of_People_World_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Not
Your
Kind
of
People
World
Tour">Not
Your
Kind
of
People
World
Tour</a>.
The
song
<i>Not
Your
Kind
of
People</i>
was
used
in
a
trailer
for
the
upcoming
video
game,
<a
href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid_V:_The_Phantom_Pain?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Metal
Gear
Solid
V:
The
Phantom
Pain">Metal
Gear
Solid
V:
The
Phantom
Pain</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-91"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
the
December
2012
issue
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone">Rolling
Stone</a></i>,
Shirley
Manson
and
Butch
Vig
announced
plans
to
enter
a
recording
studio
to
record
new
material.<sup
id="cite_ref-92"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup>
Garbage
and
<a
href="/wiki/Screaming_Females?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Screaming
Females">Screaming
Females</a>
recorded
a
cover
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Because_the_Night?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Because
the
Night">Because
the
Night</a>&quot;
for
<a
href="/wiki/Record_Store_Day?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Record
Store
Day">Record
Store
Day</a>
2013.<sup
id="cite_ref-93"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup>
They
released
a
video
directed
by
<a
href="/wiki/Sophie_Muller?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sophie
Muller">Sophie
Muller</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-94"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
May
7,
2013
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Because_the_Night?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Because
the
Night">Because
the
Night</a>&quot;
was
officially
released
as
a
single
on
iTunes.<sup
id="cite_ref-95"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
April
2013,
Vig
told
<i><a
href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
(magazine)">Billboard</a></i>
that
the
band
will
begin
recording
the
follow-up
to
<i>Not
Your
Kind
of
People</i>
in
June
2013,
and
hope
to
have
their
sixth
studio
album
out
in
2014.<sup
id="cite_ref-96"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
band
released
their
first
live
DVD,
<i><a
href="/wiki/One_Mile_High..._Live?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="One
Mile
High...
Live">One
Mile
High...
Live</a></i>,
on
May
27,
2013.<sup
id="cite_ref-97"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Shirley
Manson
confirmed
that
they
will
release
two
new
songs
for
<a
href="/wiki/Record_Store_Day?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Record
Store
Day">Record
Store
Day</a>
on
April
19,
2014.
&quot;Girls
Talk
Shit&quot;,
an
out-take
from
the
<i>Absolute
Garbage</i>
sessions,<sup
id="cite_ref-classicrock_98-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-classicrock-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-GirlsTalkShit_99-0"

href="#cite_note-GirlsTalkShit-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup>
has
been
re-recorded
to
include
vocals
from
<a
href="/wiki/Brody_Dalle?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brody
Dalle">Brody
Dalle</a>,
and
will
be
backed
by
an

from
the
<i>Not
Your

of

sessions,
&quot;Time
Will
Destroy
Everything&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-100"

href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>Garbage's
intention
is
to
make
<a
href="/wiki/Pop_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pop
music">pop</a>-like
songs
which
mixed
a
variety
of
genres,
with
Steve
Marker
saying
that
the
band
wanted
to
&quot;take
pop
music
and
make
it
as
horrible
sounding
as
we
can.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-volume_17-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-volume-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
Shirley
Manson
has
stated
that
the
band
itself
&quot;used
to
describe
[their
sound]
as
sci-fi
pop,
because
we
felt
it
was
taking
a
futuristic
approach.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-101"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup>
Vig
has
said
the
<a
href="/wiki/Crossover_(music)?qsrc=3044#Crossover_as_a_mix_of_genres"
title="Crossover
(music)">crossover</a>-heavy
sound
was
inspired
by
the
band's
background
with
remixes,
where
songs
would
be
rearranged
to
every
musical
style
to
which
they
held
interest,<sup
id="cite_ref-102"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
also
that
he
&quot;grew
up
listening
to
everything
from
pop
radio
and
opera
to
country
music
and
polka,
so
I
really
thought
that
Garbage
would
be
an
interesting
and
eclectic
thing
to
do.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-volume_17-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-volume-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
Garbage
have
been
inspired
by
<a
href="/wiki/Roxy_Music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Roxy
Music">Roxy
Music</a>,<sup

class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Pretenders">The
Pretenders</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-mmaker_104-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-mmaker-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Siouxsie_and_the_Banshees?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Siouxsie
and
the
Banshees">Siouxsie
and
the
Banshees</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-mmaker_104-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-mmaker-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-105"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a

title="Curve

<script
type="text/javascript">




render_ads(false,
window['ad_config_bot']);





function
afc_match()
{








var
count
=
-1;








if(window['ad_config_top'])
{












count
=
window['ad_config_top'];








}









var
countBottom
=
0;








if(window['ad_config_bot'])
{












countBottom
=
window['ad_config_bot'];








}









if(window['backfillParam'])
{




























window['backfillParam']['pl_bmodn']
=
5;
























window['backfillParam']['pl_tnum']
=
count;












window['backfillParam']['pl_bnum']
=
countBottom;








}


































var
_matchUrl
=
"/afc-match?q=Garbage_%28band%29&page=1&ac=24&qid=026338ED36AAE9BD7C49BE6E904F15BB&qsrc=121&dm=&qrt=2&lid="+
"&o=0&l=dir&oo=&cl=ca-aj-cat&ch=cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN";





















_matchUrl+=
"&userip=76.78.3.114";




































_matchUrl+="&losid=a&locid=encw&lodid=us&loaid=a16";









var
location
=
window.location
+
"";








location
=
location.substring(7);








var
cutIdx
=
location.indexOf("/");








if
(location.indexOf(":")
>
-1)
{




















cutIdx
=
1
+
cutIdx
+
location.substring(cutIdx+1).indexOf("/");








}









var
urlPrefix
=
location.substring(0,
cutIdx);








_matchUrl
=
"http://"
+
urlPrefix
+
_matchUrl
+
"&afcec="
+
count
+
"&afcecb="
+
countBottom;








ajax_get(_matchUrl,
null,
null);




}





function
getXHR()
{








if
(window.XMLHttpRequest)
{












return
new
XMLHttpRequest();








}
else
if
(window.ActiveXObject)
{












try
{
















return
new
ActiveXObject("Msxml2.XMLHTTP");












}
catch
(e)
{
















try
{




















return
new
ActiveXObject("Microsoft.XMLHTTP");
















}
catch
(E)
{




















return
null;
















}












}








}








else
{












return
null;








}




}





function
ajax_get(url,
onsuccess,
onerror)
{








var
obj
=
getXHR();








if(obj)
{












obj.onreadystatechange
=
function()
{
















if(obj.readyState==4)
{




















if
(obj.status
==
200
&&
typeof(onsuccess)
==
"function")
{
























onsuccess(obj);




















}
else
if
(typeof(onerror)
==
"function")
{
























onerror(obj);




















}






















try
{
























delete
obj['onreadystatechange'];




















}
catch(e)
{}
















}












};












obj.open("GET",
url,
true,
"",
"");












obj.send(null);












return
obj;








}
else
{












if(onerror)
{
















onerror("Error
creating
XHR");












}
else
{
















a10.debug("Error
creating
XHR");












}












return
null;








}




}





afc_match();

</script>
